Below is a formal, canonical definition stack for the six terms you specified.
They are defined axiomatically, relationally, and operationally, so they can be used in Nyumba Theory, OST, Mungu Theory, DAO logic, Jiwe schemas, and CivOS execution without ambiguity.

Everything is ASCII and precise.

####################################################################
CORE FORMAL PRIMITIVES OF INSTITUTIONAL & ONTIC ACTION
####################################################################

These six concepts form a strict dependency chain.
None can exist without the ones before it.

Project ‚Üí Boot ‚Üí Program ‚Üí Execution ‚Üí Cycle ‚Üí Process
====================================================================

PROJECT
====================================================================

Formal Definition
Project := Intentional Ontic Seed
A Project is the decision to bring something into being.

Axiomatic Definition
A Project exists iff:
- There is an intended outcome
- There is a declared scope
- There is a commitment to attempt realization
Structure
Project P =
{
  Purpose,
  Boundary,
  Initiator(s),
  Legitimacy Claim,
  Termination Condition
}
Properties
‚Ä¢ Exists before systems
‚Ä¢ Is not executable
‚Ä¢ Is not repeatable by default
‚Ä¢ Can fail without ever running

Nyumba Interpretation
A Project is ontic intention, not action.

Failure Mode
‚Ä¢ Vagueness
‚Ä¢ Infinite scope
‚Ä¢ No termination condition

====================================================================
2. BOOT
Formal Definition
Boot := Transition from Intent to Operability
A Boot is the first irreversible act that transforms a Project into something that can run.

Axiomatic Definition
Boot(P) occurs iff:
- Preconditions are met
- Initial state is instantiated
- Rollback is no longer free
Structure
Boot B =
{
  Initial State,
  Minimal Resources,
  Activation Signal,
  Point of No Return
}
Properties
‚Ä¢ One-time (per instance)
‚Ä¢ Irreversible
‚Ä¢ Creates identity continuity
‚Ä¢ Produces an ontic string (OST-compatible)

Nyumba Interpretation
Boot is birth.

Failure Mode
‚Ä¢ Premature boot
‚Ä¢ Boot without governance
‚Ä¢ Boot without exit conditions

====================================================================
3. PROGRAM
Formal Definition
Program := Structured Intent with Rules of Operation
A Program is the formalized logic that governs how execution is allowed to occur.

Axiomatic Definition
Program exists iff:
- Rules are explicit
- Inputs are defined
- State transitions are specified
Structure
Program G =
{
  Rules,
  Roles,
  Permissions,
  Allowed Transitions,
  Prohibited Transitions
}
Properties
‚Ä¢ Static until modified
‚Ä¢ Interpretable by humans or machines
‚Ä¢ Governs execution but does not execute

Nyumba Interpretation
The Program is law, not action.

Failure Mode
‚Ä¢ Implicit rules
‚Ä¢ Conflicting permissions
‚Ä¢ Rule drift without versioning

====================================================================
4. EXECUTION
Formal Definition
Execution := Program Applied to Reality
Execution is the actual running of a Program against real inputs and states.

Axiomatic Definition
Execution(E) occurs iff:
- A Program exists
- An actor/agent applies it
- State changes occur
Structure
Execution E =
{

FORMAL DEFINITION OF INVERTIBLE
Definition 1 ‚Äî Invertible (Core)
An operation or transformation f is invertible iff there exists a second operation f‚Åª¬π such that:

f‚Åª¬π ‚àò f = id
f ‚àò f‚Åª¬π = id
Where:

id is the identity transformation

‚àò is composition

Definition 2 ‚Äî Invertibility (Set-Theoretic)
Let:

f : A ‚Üí B
Then f is invertible iff:

Injective (no loss):

‚àÄ a‚ÇÅ,a‚ÇÇ ‚àà A, f(a‚ÇÅ)=f(a‚ÇÇ) ‚áí a‚ÇÅ=a‚ÇÇ
Surjective (no remainder):

‚àÄ b ‚àà B, ‚àÉ a ‚àà A : f(a)=b
Together:

f is bijective ‚áî f is invertible
Definition 3 ‚Äî Invertible Process (Nyumba)
A process P is invertible iff every state transition within it admits a reversal operator that restores both:

‚Ä¢ internal state
‚Ä¢ external dependencies

Formally:

‚àÄ ŒîX ‚àà P, ‚àÉ ŒîX‚Åª¬π :
  X‚ÇÄ --ŒîX--> X‚ÇÅ
  X‚ÇÅ --ŒîX‚Åª¬π--> X‚ÇÄ
STRONG VS WEAK INVERTIBILITY
Weak Invertibility
State can be restored approximately or functionally, but not identically.

f‚Åª¬π(f(x)) ‚âà x
Examples:

rollback without history

reconstruction from partial logs

‚ùå Not invertible under Nyumba law

Strong Invertibility (Canonical)
State is restored exactly, including all semantic and structural context.

f‚Åª¬π(f(x)) = x
‚úÖ Required for true invertibility.

  | NonInvertible

| ------------- | --------------------------------- |

| Weak | Approximate reversal |

f = (f·µ£ ‚äï f‚Çë)

I. E-U-S THEORY ‚Äî MINIMAL RECALL
We work inside E-U-S theory, where:

II. INVERTIBILITY IN E-U-S TERMS
Definition EUS-I ‚Äî Fully Invertible Transformation

‚àÉ T‚Åª¬π such that:
T‚Åª¬π ‚àò T (E, U, S) = (E, U, S)

U‚Ä≤ = U   (no universe memory change)

  invertible(E ‚Üí E‚Ä≤)

‚àß invertible(S ‚Üí S‚Ä≤)
